** वामगण्ड —०निहितः प्रस्फुरन् पुञ्जीतः** (here the word is appropriate as the lip is flexible and could be contracted) **यः अनरः तस्मात्समुद्रतः &c. उद्धर्षित -** horripilated. In translating we have followed the reading **उच्छ्रामित शरीरशोमां.**

** P. 155 उल्हसित &c —उल्लसिताभ्यामानन्दसाध्वसाभ्यां** (i.e. rising in turns) **विषमः यः सम्भ्रमः तेन यद्वलनं तेन यः मोहः तेन मन्थरे** dull **भ्रमन्ती च लोचने यस्याः।**

** स्नेहविभ्रम &e.**—**स्नेह विभ्रमाभ्यामुन्मिश्रं;** Trip reads **विभ्रमोजितं —विभ्रमेण ऊर्जितं** (beautiful).

** मालतीप्रियसखी** —She means—Being Mal.'s dear friend and her constant companion, she must have noticed such things in the case of Mâl, who was in a similar condition and so she can ask but such questions only. The side meaning is. If you confess this, Lav. will not expose yon as she did not Mâlati.You can freely confess your love for Mak. to us.

** P 156 निःसङ्गठन &c.—निर्गतः सङ्गः यस्मिन् कर्मणि तथा तथा** (in a M. N. 6 manner not to be attracted by any thing else) **लग्ने निश्चले च**। Trip. reads **निसर्ग** (naturally) **लग्न .**

** मन्मथबलात्कारितः—मन्मथबलात्कारः सञ्जातोस्य** Forcibly incited by passion. **कन्दर्पजननी—**(1) The inflamer of his passion; (2) the mother of Pradyumna.

 Rukminî was the daughter of Bhishmaka, king of the Vidarbhas (the modern Berar. Kundinapura was its capital). Although solicited in marriage by Krishna, her brother Rukmi, who was jealous of Krishna and therefore hostile to the match, arranged her marriage with S'is'upâla, king of Chedi. Rukmini, however, who in her heart loved Krishna, sent a letter to him in which she requested him to take her away. Krishna came and assisted by Balarâma carried her off as she proceeded to offer her devotions at a temple. They were hotly pursued but in the battle that ensued, Rukmi was struck to the ground, but his life was spared by Krishna at his sister's intercession.

** का प्रतिपत्ति—**What course will you adopt; how will you act? **प्रतिपत्ति** is the knowledge and decision of the course of action to be followed or the steps to be taken; cf. **बिषादलुप्तप्रतिपत्ति** Rag. III. 40. Kum V. 42 & Màl. p. 88.

** P. 157. दुष्टशार्दूलकवलनात्—**Trip. **—मृत्युकवलात् कृत्यकर—**According to Dr. Bhán.—possession, property; according to Jag, a prize set apart at a game. In this case the meaning will be-This person is his in as much as he won me as a prize at the dangerous game he played with the tiger and saved me.

** स्मरिष्यसि एतद्वचनम्—**Bud. means that she might act differently in Mak's presence through bashfulness or under excitement, which she should not do.

** द्वितीयप्रहर॰—द्वितीयप्रहरस्य नाडिकास्तासां विच्छेदः—**the termination of the ghatikâs making up the second prahara or watch. This may also mean the close of each of the ghatikas of the second watch; but this does not seem to be intended, as the drum was generally beaten at the end of a Prahara. Trip. reads **द्वितीययामविच्छेदः** which makes the meaning clear.

** P. 158. कथितप्रणय॰—(1) कथितः प्रणयरूपः प्रसादो यस्य** Your favour in the shape of your love for whom has been declared by you; or **कथितप्रणय एव प्रसादो यस्य** who has received the favour of the declaration of your love. **एव तव दासः अस्ति.**

** प्रेयान् &c.—The fig. is कारणममुच्चय.**

** P. 159.ऊजितं—**adv. in a noble or glorious manner. **वान्यवघूरा-बान्धवस्य धूः।**The yoke (burden, responsible task) to be borne by kinsmen. Fig.-may be **पर्यायोत्क.**

** निशीथ॰—निशीथे निःसञ्चारस्तेन रमणीयता.**

** उपरिवलभी॰—**May be taken as one word like **उपर्यलिन्दक** p. 45; having moved through the lofty windows of the top-rooms of mangious. **परिणत** **—**old; **परिणतसुराया** **गन्धसंस्कारः गर्भे यस्य**

** P. 160. मुहुः &c.—आमोद-आमोदः सोतिनिर्हारी** (extremely pleasing). Amar - **मुहुरुपचितोत एव स्फारः कर्पूरवासो यस्य**. Fig. **अनुमान.**

 \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

Act. VIII.

**——¤——**

** P. 161.ग्रीष्मदिवसावसान&c.—**The bath to be taken in the evening. Here although Avalokita speaks of the evening bath, it must have been taken at a late hour-probably an hour or so before mid-night. For as Mádh. and Màl, together with Avalokità, are conversing just after having finished their ablution which Mâdh calls **प्रत्यय** (see further on **प्रत्यग्र सायन्तनस्नान**), Mad., Lavangiká and others come from Nandana's house, and it is then past midnight as is clear from Bud.'s words (: &c.) at the end of the seventh Act. And we cannot suppose either the bath or the conversation to have lasted for five or six hours. Again Avalokitâ says that she comes after having saluted Kám. then just returned from Naudana's house. And we know from the prologue to the VIIth Act that when Kám left Nandana's house the night was pretty well advanced. So we conclude that the bath was taken an hour or so before midnight.

** निशीथस्य—निशीथ** the midnight; **नितरां शेरतेऽस्मिन्** fr. **शी** with **नि** and aff **थ**. The reading **निशीथिनीनाथस्य** is rejected because the epithet **प्रौढसुहृदः** and the words **यौवनश्री** go against it while they are peculiarly happy in the case of **निशीथ**. In the following sl. the moon is described as just rising and so it can not be in its Yauvana. Again as shown above it was midnight to which the description belongs.

** दलयति &c.—प्राक्प्रकाशः** the early light i.e. when the moon was just about to rise or was on the horizon. This is necessary to make it comparable with **परिशुष्यत्प्रौढताली** leaf. **मन्दमन्द—**is necessary that the moonlight should be mistaken for the pollen.**मकरन्द॰** v. l. will mean—mixed with floral juice, heavy and hence by implication, moving gently. This reading is better as it is more poetical and as there is nothing to correspond to **मन्दo** in the first two lines; cf. with this Kâli.'s beautiful description of the moonrise when at hand –**उदयगूढशशाङ्कमरीचिभिः** &c Vik. III. 6. Fig. Utprekshá.

** वामशीलां—**merely means, obstinate, unyielding; it has not got its usual bad sense here as in a gay: (Sâk. IV. or infra in IX. 8.**उपावर्तये**—Make her turn to me, to act agreeably to my wishes, win her over.

** P. 162.निश्चोतन्ते—**The Atm. is unusual. The poet uses the correct Pada in his Uttar. (**एतास्ता मधुनो धाराः श्चोतन्ति सविषास्त्वयि)** III. 84, **कबरी॰—i.e.कबरीजल, सान्द्र॰—**A Bah. **oकोद्भेदा,** instead of the Matub aff. a, would have been better for the sake of brevity; but the use of. **वत्** may be defended; see Jag,**अङ्कपालीम्पाली** (**पालि** is more usual; **पालयति पाल्यते अनेन अनया वा** fr. **पाल् + अच् + इ**) means a region; hence-large and fleshy lap**;वितर**—give me your lap i. e. a seat on it; hence an embrace (**आश्लेषं** **देहीत्यर्थः**) as shown by the context. Fig.—Samuchchaya.

** निरनुरोध—**Seeing no inclination on her part to comply with his request, he addresses her thus **निर्गत अनुरोधः** (regard for, consideration; hence, compliance with)**:यस्याः** one not yielding to one's wishes, regardless. **नीरनुरोधे—**V. 1. pitiless, hard- hearted. See p. 185.

** जीवयन्निव—**Sl. occurring in Uttar. also (with the reading **ससाध्वसश्रम** for **समूढसाध्वस**) It is, however, in its proper place here. **समूढ**—grown **ऐन्द्रव** &c.—**इन्दोः इमे** **ऐन्द्रवाः ये मयूखाः तैः चुम्बितः अतएव, तेषां चुम्बितेन वा स्यन्दते असौ स्यन्दनशीलः यः चन्द्रमणिहारस्तस्य इव विभवो यस्य।** Fig. **निदर्शना** and **व्यतिरेक (ऐन्दवेत्यादिना सादृश्यमुक्त्वा जीवयन्निवेति विशेषस्योक्तेः **Virarághava on Uttar).

** संविभाग—**Participation in, joining in.

** दग्धं &c—मलयानिल** - of. Mal's speech at p. 132 **(चन्द्रातपमलयमारुतः &c) चन्द्रपादैः - cf. विसृजति हिमगर्भैरनिमिन्दुर्मयुखैः।** Sak. III. 8. तु—As to as regards; cf**.चन्द्रोपरागं प्रति तु केनपि विप्रलब्धासि** Mud. I. As to, **तु**—but.**आमतo**—This is put in to explain why his ear was pained. It was pained on account of the note of the cuckoo stirring up his passion. Cf. however, Kálidása-**एवं गतेपि प्रियेव में मञ्जुस्वनेति न कोपोस्यां (परभृतायां)** Vik. IV. Oc—The foolish Kokila, thinking that its voice imitates the sweet music of your voice, utters its notes; but they are discordant to my ears; your voice alone, Kinnar-like, can please them. cf ** स्वरेण तस्याममृतस्रुतेव प्रजल्पितायामभिजातवाचि। अप्यन्यपुष्टा प्रतिकूलशब्दा श्रोतुर्वितन्त्रीरिव ताड्यमाना।**Kum. 1. 45 - The fig. is **पर्यायोक्त.**

** P. 163. अनिर्वहणशीले—निर्वहण** carrying out or putting into execution one's plans &c.; here Màl.'s desire to request Màdh. to embrace her**.विच्छर्दित—** entirely set aside or given up; see p. p. 144, 150.

** सासूयं—**Because she betrayed her. Or perhaps Ava. attríbuted to Màl. what she never said but which she would not have the courage to deny in the presence of her lover and hence her which Màdh, admires in the next speech**,सर्वतोमुखं -** lit. facing all directions; able to meet every case. **वैदग्ध्यं —विदग्धस्य भावः। विदग्ध—**lit what is well burnt, polished or refined; hence well cultured, skilful.

** P. 161. अनवसित्तार्थ॰—अनवसितमत एवार्थे मन्थरम्** slow to express i. e. not expressing the full sense as it was not finished**.चारुता -** Because the curiosity to hear it was thereby increased.

** बाष्पाम्भसा &.—कान्त्यमृतं कान्तिरेवामृतं.** Fig. Rûpaka. **निवेशिता ०—निवेशिताः मयुख एयं मृणालदण्डः येन.** The lunar ray is the lotus-stalk which is hollow and like a tube and the moon is supposed to drink the nectar by means of it by the process of suction. Fig. A blending of Utprekshi and Rûpaka **(अङ्गाङ्गिभावेन सङ्करः).**

** उच्छकित—** see Jag; it rather means 'gushing forth'; see p. 148; 73 **(उच्छलत). बाष्पोत्पीड-** stream or burst of tears see p. 131) **तेन मन्थरं यथा स्यात्तथा।**

** उदर्कः—**may be derived fr. **अर्क्** or **ऋच्** to praise or **अर्च्** to worship. **उदर्क्यते, उदृच्यते, उदर्च्यते वा**, and means the final reward, fruit; **उदकैः फलमुत्तरम्।** Amara.

** P. 165 वर्धयति—**(more usually **वर्धापयति**) Lit, to enrich or canse to prosper; hence to express one's satisfaction or joy at such prosperity, to congratulate one upon**.प्रथमदर्शना—०दर्शने या अभिषङ्गः** strong emotion or attachment.

** विस्तारिस्तन॰—स्तनौ कुम्भौ स्तनकुम्भौ विस्तारिणी स्तनकुम्भौ कुड्मला इव स्तनकुम्भकुड्मलौ तयोः भरः** bulk, sizo, **तस्य उत्सङ्गः** the surface **तस्मिन्,** or **विस्तारी यः स्तन—भरः &c. भर fr. भृ** to fill + **अ (च्)** fulness **(पूर्णता)**, bulk, mass, as here and in lX. 24; also excess **(अतिशयः)** as in VI. 17. **उत्सङ्ग—**Jag takes this in the sense of **क्रोड** i. e. **भुजान्तर** the space between the arms, bosom), and has recourse to an awkward Bah. It is better to take it in the sense of ‘the surface of'; **उत्सङ्ग—**fr. **सञ्ज्** with **उत्+अ** **(घञ)** added in the sense of **आधार** or support-means the lap; hence surface, as in **दुषदो वासितोत्सङ्गाः** Rag. IV. 74. Or it may simply mean, contact, union.

** पाणिपीडन —**Lit. seizing the hand firmly, so as not to let go the grasp; hence, marrying; of. **न प्रमाणीकृतः पाणिः बाल्ये बालेन पीडितः।** Uttar. VII. 5. **सर्वस्वदायीकृता —सर्वस्वस्य दायः सर्वस्वदायः न स॰ असवस्वदायः; असर्व॰ सर्व॰ सम्पद्यते तथा कृता** given in place of everything.

** P. 166.पदशब्द इव—**Something like a tread of footsteps. **दिष्ट्या वधंसे —**Lit you rise by your good luck; you are to be eongratulated upon,**दिष्टि** means good luck, any fortunate occur- rence or an auspicious event;- **वृध्दि** means one's expressing joy at another's good fortune; cf. **दिष्टिवृद्धिमिव शुश्राव दिष्टिवृद्धिसम्भ्रमो** &c. Kàd. Hence **दिष्टया ** (regarded as an indec.) has come to be used with **वृध्** in the sense of-to be congratulated upon.

** निव्यूढः —**see p. 91**.सम्भावनाभार—**responsibility of the trust reposed in (the weighty business entrusted to) her by Kámanda- kî. **सम्भावना** lit. means honouring one as by entrusting a business to one Cf ** सिध्यन्ति कर्मसु महत्त्वपि यन्नियोज्याः सम्भावनागुणमेवैहि तमीश्वराणाम् S′k. VII. 4.अभियोगः —** collision, attack. We have already got the word in the sense of close application to (p 18), energetic effort &c. I. 34. (p. 38).

** P. 167.अतुलo **—;**प्रणेय लालस** indicates habit-always delighting in. **साहसे—**in an adventure. Cf **गजेनेव शैवालकवलग्रासलालसः** **करः** Kad. ०**सस्याहवे—**is another reading; but the context requires **साहसेकृणत्—**merely means here rattling against (the bones of elephants). **स्फुटत् &c.—स्फुटन् यः करटः तस्य कोटरात्... स्थितानामस्थ्नां दलने एकवीरः** (the only one able to do it; pre-eminently fitted to do it).**वीर** when compounded with **एक** should be**वीरैक** as it ought to take. **पूर्वनिपात **(precedence), by Pân II. 1. 58; but **एकविर** which is more often used by poets may be defended by supposing that the operation of the rule above mentioned is not universal-**कयमेकवीर इति। पूर्वकालैकेति बाधित्वा परत्वादनेन समासे वीरैक इति हि स्यात्। बहुलग्रहणाद्भविष्यति।** Sid. Kan. Fig **अपरतुतप्रशंसा** and **अनुप्रास.**

** विक्रान्तप्लुतं —**Jag. takes this as acc. governed by **विलसतः** but against grammar as **विलस्** is intransitive. It must be taken as an adv comp**; विक्रान्तानि प्लुतानि यस्मिन्कर्माणि तद्यथा तथा**। Manoevering boldly, making heroic movements.

** P. 168. बाक्स्तम्भं—** Because she was deprived of her power of speech by Kapâlakundalá by hor mystic power. **सक्रोधहासं—हास** at Mal's helplessness as she could not speak.

** कन्याविटः—**The despoiler of a maiden **(कन्यादूषक)** who is to protect you (a side-meaning of **पति**; see Jag.). The speech is of course, sarcastic **चिरात्** — and so the vengeance will be terrible.

** निकृत्य—**Fr. **कृत्** 6 conj. to cut, with **नि.**

** P. 169. सम्भावितः —**approached by you, found out.

** सावक्षेपा॰ —सावक्षेपं यया तथापविद्धौ** (tossed or cast about) **यो विकटौ ऊरुदण्डो ताभ्यां निष्ठुरं** fiercely **यथा तथा। साधिक्षेपं **(treating the danger or enemy with contempt). **दूरनिक्षेपाविद्धौ (दूरनिक्षेपे आविद्धौ** stretched so as to take long strides) &c. will be a better reading **सञ्जात॰—सजातो मत्सराधिक्षेपौ यस्य** (feeling jealous and insulted).

** P. 170. सङ्घट्टदुर्गमात्—सङ्घट्टेन दुर्गमः तस्मात्** that in which passage out was difficult owing to the collision or encounter; hence a hard and close fight. **निर्मलनिरन्तर॰—निर्मलाश्च ते निरन्तरं (निर्गतमन्तरं यस्मिन्कर्मणि तथा) उद्धृताश्च धौता**: &c. **मदलीला &c. — मदलीलया कलितः** (lit. seized; hence influenced) **तस्य विकटभुजदण्डेन आविद्धः यः हलः तस्य हेलया विक्षुभितमत एव उद्वेल्लिततरङ्ग (उद्वेल्लिताः तरङ्गा यस्य) यत् &c. कलिन्दतनया**— Daughter of the mountain Kalinda or Yama i. e. Yamuna.

 Allusion—On one occasion Balaráma, wishing to bathe in the Jamuna from which he was at some distance, called upon the river,. when elevated with wine, to come to him. His command not being obeyed he plunged his ploughshare into it and dragged the water to him until the river, in a human form, asked his forgiveness and proinised good behaviour in future. See Bg. P. X. 65; V. P. V. 25. This incident is often alluded to by Sans. poets. of. **उन्मदहलिहलापकर्षणभयप्रपलायितामिव यमुना** &c. Kad.

** विकट &c. —विकटं विशृङ्खलं (विगता श्रृङ्खला** restraint **यस्मिन्कर्मणि) च यथा तथा उत्पतितः निर्दयः अमन्दः** (moving quickly) **च यः मकरन्दस्तस्य व्यतिकरण** (on account of) यः क्षोभः ते**न विकला ये प्रतियोधाः तेषां परिवर्तनेन उद्भुत ...वकाशं विशङ्कलितः** (pervading**)** **कलकलः यत्र। विशङ्कलित** —The readings in the foot-note **—** **अवसरत्, विकसत्** mean-moving, spreading about.

 P. 171. **भीषण** &c,—** भीषणः यः भुजः वज्र इव भुजवज्रः तेन जर्जरिताः पथर येषां ते–ज॰** **अतएव अवसन्नाः** (drooping, unnerved) **ये सुभटाः तेषां हस्तेभ्यः** '... निवहेन घातितं कृताघातं (struck down, wounded) **यदशेषं... सञ्चार एव निवर्तितं विषमं साहसं येन।** This passage is differently read and it is very difficult to see which is the original reading, The Nir, Ed. reads**— वज्रखचितपञ्जरपर्यस्तसमरविमुखसुभट... युधोपरुद्धाशेषरिपुसैन्यविकटापसारव्यतिरिक्तमार्ग॰**. The reading in Dr. Bhán. Ed. is **oपञ्जरोपसन्न (वसन्न** seems to be better)... **विविधायुधोपमर्दसमवसारित** (this is preferable to **घातित) सैनिकनिकरं पदातिरिक्तमार्ग॰** (which, however, should not have been separated from the preceding, since **पदातिरिक्तमार्गसञ्चार** is no **साहस).**

 **सौध॰— प्रतिहारेण करणेन** (through the door—keeper) विनयोपन्यासेन (by sending a conciliatory message) **प्रशमितं विशेषसङ्कटं येन।** The King asked the go **प्रº** to go to Madh. and Mak. and to pacify them by using mild words and so got the evil of enmity averted. मपनीत॰ **उपनीतौ माधव्न्दौ तयोः। प्रस्फुरत् प्रस्फुरती मत्सरवैलक्ष्ये एव मषी तया। भूरिवसुनन्दनौ प्रतिबोध्य।** P. 172 **प्रेयसः —**of my dear friend (and not **प्रीतस्य** as Jag takes it). **निर्व्याज—** natural

 ** दोर्निप्पेष** &c.— The cons. is **प्राक् वीरान् दो॰लम् उन्मथ्नतः ततो ताननुपात्य **&c **विक्रामतः प्रेयसः पन्थाः। दोर्भ्यां यः निष्पेषः** (crushing) **तेन विशीर्णः यः (अस्थि)** सञ्चयस्तेन दलन्ति **कङ्कालानि यथा तथा। उद्वेल्लत्** &c.**– उद्वेलन्तः ये... खण्डाः तेषां** **निकरैः आकीर्णस्य। द्वेधा** &c. As Madh dashed forward, the soldiers on either side remained pinned to the ground being paralysed with fear &c.

** इन्दुमयूख—** Probably wine was drunk after being exposed to the moonlight Cf. **न च शशिप्रतिमाभरणं मधु।** Rag. IX. 7. **भुजार्गल— मुजः अर्गल इव l**it, an arm like a bar; huge and muscular. **असारविधुराम्—असारा अत एव विधुराः; असारेण विधुरा वा तान् विधुर —** Properly unable to bear a burden i. e. responsibility **(विगता धूः कार्यभारो यस्य);** hence helpless, pitiable. See p. 181 also Fig. **निदर्शना.**

 ** सस्मितमालती** &c**. — मालत्या वलितः यः लोलः कटाक्षः तेन पराहतं** caused to be withdrawu. **सस्मित—** not on hearing of the fight, as Jag. has it, but on hearing how Mad.'s secret was tricked out of her and how she was made to elope with Makaranda.

 P. 13 **ममहि** &c. —**अनिष्टैकबुद्धेः—अनिष्टमेव एकं तस्य बुद्धिः तद् बुद्धौ वा यस्य।** This was because of his past experience; or because **प्रेम पश्यति मयान्यपदेपि** Kir IX. 70. **द्रवति हृदयं —** The heart is generally described as melting through pity and not through anguish, and so we should rather expect **दलति** for **द्रवति.** The reading of Jag, therefore, given in the foot—note, should be substituted for this. My internal soul is fluttering within me continuously through agitation.' Fig. **समुच्चय.**

 P. 174. **कलयसि—** If you wish to know or guage (test) my love. **अविज्ञाय —** Without knowing the true state of things.

 P. 175. **याता भवेत्** &c. — Jag.'s interpretation of this is not satisfactory. The doubts are **मालती भगवतीभवनं याता भवेत् किं** and **जीवन्त्युपेष्यति वा** (supposing she did not go to Kam.' dwelling). **सौदामिनीº — T**he word Saudaminí is purposely used to suggest the entrance of Sau. at the beginning of the next Act. see Jag. Fig.— **अथर्थान्तरन्यास.**

**ACT IX.**  
**<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-172408700331.png"/>**

 P. 176. **भगवतः —** Sau. speaks of the mountain with Venerntion as being the seat of the attainmen**t of miraculous power by the practice of Yoga and also of मन्त्रसिद्धि. See Jag. तथाह मुत्पतिता —** She again rises into the sky in search of Madh. and makes this observation.

 **पद्मावती —** situated at the confluence of the Pará (Parbati) and Sindhu (Sindh) at a distance of about 25 miles from Narwar, in Mâlwa (see notes p. 14) seems to have been a beautiful city from the description given here-adorned with fine palaces and mansions, magnificient temples, city-gates and turrets &c. The Parbati joins the Sindhu from the left while the river Mohvar or Madhuvar (probably the Madhunati of the play) joins it from the right at some distance further from the junction of the two. The Lavana (now called Lun) is also in the vicinity joining the Sindhu,

 **उतुङ्गसौध** &0.— This gives an idea of what the old Indian cities generally used to be. **गोपुर —** A city—gate (with a tower on either side) **पुरद्वारं तु गोपुरं** Amara. It is derived as **गोपायति (पुरं)** fr. **गुप् + उर,** Or **गवां पुरं —** Originally so called because the king's cattle were probable kept there in stalls attached to it. **अह—**a turret, a buttress**, उत्तुङ्गसौधानां... पुराणां चाट्टाः तैः आदौ पाटितं पश्चाद्विमुक्तं,** Fig. **—अपह्नुति** based on Utprekha. The currents of the two rivers are very happily compared here to pieces of the sky detached from the main body by the piercing turrets and so fallen down.

** गोगर्भिणी॰— गावश्च ताः गर्भिण्यश्च i . e .** . **गर्भिण्यः गावः** cows with calf. The word **गो** takes **पूर्वनिपात** i, e. stands first in the comp. (iustead of standing as the second member) by the Sûtra '**चतुष्पादो** **गर्भिण्या'** Pàn.II. 1. 71. i. e, a noun expressive of a quadruped may optionally take **पूर्वनि॰** when compounded with the word **गर्भिणी, मालभारि॰** see Jag. The final **आ** of **माला** is shortened by **इष्टकेषिका** &c. Paa. VI. 3. 65. (quoted by Jag.). So **डष्टकचितं** and **इषीकतूलम्;** ** ºभारिण्यः अत एव सेव्याः** &०

 P. 177. **अम्बुगर्भ॰**—**अम्बु गर्भे यस्य अत एव गम्भीरः** ६० **हेरम्ब** &c.—The fig. is Upamâ . **तरुण** &c.—**तरुणाः** (a kind of tree) **च कदम्बाश्च;** or **तरुणाः** (young) **च ते कदम्बाश्च जम्ब्बश्च तासां वनैः अवनद्धः** (held or kept confined within) **अन्धकारः येषु एतादृशा गुरवः निकुञ्जाः येषु। एतादृक्षु गम्भीरगह्वरेषु उद्गारो यस्याः or गह्वरेषु य उद्गारस्तेनोपलक्षिता गोदावरी तथा मुखरिताश्च ताः स्निग्धाश्च ता विशालाश्च मेखलाभुवः येषु तान्।** The N. Ed. reads **गुरुगिरिनिकुञ्जगुञ्जद्गम्भीरगद्गदोद्गारघोषणगोदावरी** &c. Cf. with this the description in the Uttar. I. **अयमविरलानोकहनिवहनिरन्तर- स्निग्धनीलपरिसरारण्यपारणद्धगोदावरीमुखरकन्दरः... गिरिः** &c. p. 27.

 ** अपौरुषेयप्र॰—**i . e the Linga had appeared there spontaneously and was not made and consecrated by man.

 **अखिलधरद—**Jag., takes this as an epithet of निगम, but it is better to take it separately as an epithet of the god.

 P. 178. **संसफ—**Lit, mixed or mingled, confused; or continuons. **अनोकह—**a** **tree; **अनसः शकटस्य अकः गति हन्तीति.**

 **दधतीति**—The saine occurs in Uttar. (II. 21) and Mv. (V. 41). कुहर—कुहरं गह्वरे छिद्रे इति रत्नमाला. गुरूणि—may also mean 'prolonged'. **अम्बूकतं—**Properly the sound of the splashing of water; then a sound resembling that, a growl. **अम्बुशब्दः उपचारात्तद्वति। अनन्यु अम्बु कृतम् अम्बूकृतं** Ohvi. **स्त्यान—Maguitude, depth, भावप्रधानो निर्देशः। शिशिर॰—विकीर्ण-**torn asunder; **विशीर्ण** V. 1. is better, **स्त्यायते—**Virarághava in his com, on the Mv. thus comments on this—**मूर्तद्रव्ययोग्यायाः सङ्घातभावभजनक्रियाया अमूर्तेन गुणेन गन्धेन करणवर्णनात्**—**कर्तरि कर्मव्यतीहारे इत्यात्मनैपदम्। अन्ययोग्यक्रियाया अन्येन करणं हि कर्मव्यतीहारः। अतिशयोक्तिरलङ्कारः।**

 **उद्गतदले—**implies that the tree could afford good shade. **शिम्बि—**Bee Jag. **शिम्बीनां चुम्बितमेषामस्तीति तादृशानि मुखानि यासां.**

 P. 179. **प्रविक्षिप्तं—**Violently tossed about by misgivings, disturbed by thoughts, **अन्धतमर्स— अन्धं च तत्तमः; अ ** is added to **तमस्** when preceded by **अन्धं,** **सम्** and **अव.**

 P. 180. **अविज्ञाततत्वं— अविज्ञातं तत्त्वं** your true state **यस्मिन्कर्मणि तद्यथा तथा। अद्भुतं—**adv.

 **स्वयमागृहीत** &c*f . * **समयः स वर्तत इवैष यत्र मां समनन्दयत्सुमुखि गौतमार्पितः। अयमा॰** as in the text (Uttar. I. 18)

 ** सरस॰— क्षाम** properly, emaciated, thin; hence delicate. Probably the poet had the word **क्षामत्व** in his mind and wanted to say 'with limbs like withering juicy (tender) flowers. **तृणमिव—cf. तृणमिव वने शून्ये त्यक्ता** Uttar. 111. 32. Fig. Sara.

 P. 181. **विकलकरणैः—** In which (the power of) the senses was overpowered or paralysed; or **विफल** may mean' unnerved, drooping' **०करुणैः** . 1. means **विकलानि** out of tune, discordant; or helpless **च तानि करु**णानि च. We have the same expression in Uttar. II. 28. **मर्मच्छेद॰— ममैच्छेदस्य इव या व्यथा तया विधुरैः** (over— whelmed with or pitiable on account of); see supra Il 3, p. 172. विधुर also means in a pitiable position; cf. **पुत्रशोकविधुरो धरणीशः** Udar. VII. 1. **विधुरां ज्वलनातिसर्जनात्** Kum IV. 32. **स्नेहाकूतं—**an emo— tional state of the heart full of or brought on by love; **स्नेहप्रायं स्नेहजनितं वा आकूतं; आकूत** means emotion, a feeling. Cf. **वयःस्नेहाकूतव्यतिकरघनो यत्र मदनः**। Uttar. VI. 35. **भावाकूर्त** Amaru. 4. साकूर्त p. 82.

** सावेगं—** Mark how the memory of his beloved intensifies his anguish and canses poignant pain.

 ** दलति** &c.— This sl. recurs verbatim in the Uttar., being 31st of the 3rd Act. **गाढोद्वेगं—** accounts for the **दलनक्रिया. द्विधा न तु भिद्यते—** The heart is reft but is not broken into two parts. Thus there is **विरोधाभास** here and in the following lines; see Jag. **(यद्दलति तन्न भिद्यते) विकलः—** Shattered. **कायः—** See Jag, Fig. There is also **विशेषोक्ति** in this since the causes are stated and yet the results do not follow. Sl. quoted in S D. as an instance of **खेद** (lassitude) produced by the workings of the mind **(मनश्चेष्टासमुत्पन्नः श्रमः खेद इति स्मृतः।**

 ** निरवग्रहं — अवग्रह** restraint, check. This is owing to **विधातुर्वामत्व** sre p. 179.

 P. 182. **उत्राल** &c.**— उद्गतानि नालानि येषां तानि उन्नालानि यानि बालकमलानि तेषामाकरः।** C.f I. 33. **मांसल—** Cf. **बहलपरिमकोद्गारसंवलनमसृणमांसल** &c. p. 76**. शीकरतुषार—** Jag. takes **तुषार** in the sense of 'cool'; but it in better to take it in the sense of 'spray, a mist of'; **शीकराणां शीकरा एन वा तुषाराः तैः जडः (अत एव शीतलः** by implication). Cf . **पृक्तस्तुबारैनिरिनिर्झराणां** &c. Rag. II. 13.

आक्षिपामि— change the drift of his thoughts, change the subject of his ruminations.

 ** एतस्मिन्** ६०.— Sl. occurring in the Uttar. with the last line read as **सन्दृष्टाः कुवलयिनो भुवौ विभागाः** to suit the context thare (1. 31). It is, however, in its proper place there. The poet probably inserted it here, with the necesessy change in the fourth line, after he had composed the Uctar. We should reasonably expect Mak, to ask his friend to check the flow of tears rather than to go on weeping and observing the beauty of the lake between the fall of one and the uprise of the next stream of tears. Jag. reads the last line as **दृश्यन्तां कुवलयिनो भुवो** &c. But this reading, as also Jag.' explanation, are quite out of place here. **कुवलयिनः** (looking like; having, blue lotuses) is quite inappropriate after Mak. distinctly tells his friend that the parts of the lake are full of white lotuses.

 ** मल्लिकाक्ष—**a kind of swan with the beak and legs of a blackish colour. **प्रतिपत्तिशून्यं— प्रतिपत्या शून्यः यथा तथा** not knowing what to do; or **प्रतिपत्ति** may mean 'apprehension."

 P 183. **सुमनसां— सुमनस्** a kind of Jati (Málati); or flowers. **उन्मीलत्** १० **उन्मीलन्ति।** कुटजान्येव **प्रहासः,** (the flowers being white) **स विद्यते एषाम्। मेधैर्वितानाय्यते—** is an Upama.

 ** जृम्भा॰— जृम्भा** opening, blooming. **जर्जर—**close pressed **डिम्ब—** the cluster of the buds; **तेषां डम्वरेण घना** great, enhanced **श्रीः विद्यते एषां तादृशः कदम्बद्रुमा यासु। केतक—** Jag.' 8 **केतकवृक्षाः** is strange.

 P. 184**. दुरालोक॰ दुर** goes with **रमणीयः आलोके दुःखन रमणीयाः** and is equivalent in sense to **दुरालोकरमणीयत्वाः** whose beauty it is painful to look at.

 ** पौरस्त्य—पुरो भवः पौरस्त्यः** fr. **पुरस्+त्य** by **दक्षिणापश्चात्पुरस्त्यक्।** Pan. IV. 2. 2०; ५० **दाक्षिणात्य, पाश्चात्य स्खलित—**diglodged (and tossed up) from their bed. **धर्माम्भो॰—** The first sense given by Jag is the beat; **घर्माम्भसो विगपागमौ तयोः** &० His second interpretation may be possible. **घर्माम्भसः निगमः आगमः च तयोः व्यतिकरः.** As the heat of the sultry season was not yet annihilated, perspiration disappeared when thore was a shower and a cool breeze blew but broke out agnin as the heat increased. In this case, however, the word श्री has no propriety. Cf. **नववारिधरोदयादहोभिर्भवितव्यं च निरातपद्धिरम्यैः**। Vik. IV. 3.

 P. 185. **हेति— हन्ति अनया अनेन वा** (m f.) a weapon; a bow. ह**रिहेति—**The bow of Indra, rain—bow.

 **कलह—**Mixed sounds.

 **निरनुक्रोशा—**pitiless; **निर्गतः अनुक्रोशः यस्याः। अनुक्रोश** fr. **कुश्** with **अनु;** lamenting along with; showing sympathy; hence pity. compassion.

 **अपहस्तित—** P. p. of the denom. from **अपहस्त (अपसारणार्थः हस्तः अपहस्तः)**; Lit, cast away with the hand, hence cast aside, given up, diecarded **मातर्मातर्** &c— Same as Uttar. III. 38. (where the fret line, however, begins with **हाहा देवि स्फुटति . सीदन्—**dis. tressed, writhing with pain. C. **सीदति में हृदये** Kad. **सीदन्ति मम गात्राणि** Bg. 1. 23. **विश्वक् —** (adv.) from all sides, it may also be an adj **(विश्वमषति)** stupor overpowering all senses; the adv., how— ever, is preferable.

 P. 186. **बन्धुता—**all kinsmen;ता is added in the sense of a collection' t० **ग्राम, जन, बन्धु** and **सहाय (हृदयस्य) कौमुदीमहः **moon-light festival celebrated on the 15th of A's'vin (and not Kartika, as Jag has it)

 **गात्रेषु** &c.—The fig in this sl, is Rupaka.

 P. 187. **पोत—** polished. राजपट्ट a kind of sapphire or lapis lazuli (as it must be of an azure colour).

** प्रियावार्ताहरं—** This idea is doubtless suggested by Kali's Meghaduta.

 **फलभर॰—**This line occurs in Uttar. II. 20. and Mv. V 40. **प्ररिणाह—**ripening **निकुञ्जेषु स्खलनं तेन** &c. **स्रवन्तीमुत्तरेण** To the north of the river. Words ending in **एन** govern the Acc. or the Gen.1 See Pan. II. 3. 31. and Sid. Kau. on it: Gr. § 448 (a). **दक्षिणेन ग्रामं ग्रामस्य वा। दक्षिणेन वृक्षवाटिकां** S'nk. I. **अपरि** &c.— These two lines are the same as those of Mv. V. 42 (with the readings **आप च** for **उपरि,** and **विघटमानप्रौ॰)**

 **विघटमानः— विविधं घटमानः** (used intransitively) forming into, assuming, different shapes (as soted upon by the wind). **उपचित॰—** V. 1, **उपचिता घना माला येषां **(growing in thick lines) **तादृशा ये प्रौढाः तापिच्छाः तद्न्नील।**

 ** कच्चित्सौम्य** &c.— This sl. and the mode of addressing a clond are in the Kalidasian style. **कच्चित्सौम्य** is also the beginning of a al, in Kali.'s Megh. (11.53). **प्रियसहचरी—** Lightning is often so spoken of by Sans, poets; cf. **माभूदेवं क्षणमपि च ते विद्युता विप्रयोगः।** Megh. 11. 54. **प्रथमाः—** It is difficult to see the propristy of this word, perhaps we may take the comp. as **आवीर्भूतप्रयणाश्च ते सुभगाश्च ** (fortunate now that they can get water). **मुखर** V. I. wonld be more appropriate,

 **साधुसंवाहनाभिः—** of. **मन्दं मन्दं नुदति पवनश्चानुकूलो यथा त्वां** Megh. **विश्वं विजत्** &a—The line, as it stands, presents some difficulty of meaning. Jag.'s first way is the best. Doubtless the poet meant to say— **सुरधनुः तव लक्ष्म शोभां तनोति किम्** but then **विभ्रत्** hanga loose in the sentence. Perhaps the cons. is **सुरपतिधनुः विश्वक् तव लक्ष्म बिभ्रत् तव शोभां** &c. Does the rainbow, every where becoming thy mark, enhance thy beauty? The reading **विश्वग्विष्कक्** noticed by Dr. Bhandarkar removes the difficulty**— सुरपतिधनुः तव लक्ष्म विष्वक् विष्वक्** (wherever thou goest) **तव शोभां तनौति किम्.** One com.— takes **विभ्रत्** as Voc. sing. O cloud, bearing &o.

 P. 188. **प्रतिरव** &c.— **प्रतिरवेण** (i. e. of the rumbling of the clouds) **भरिता याः कन्दरास्ताभिरानन्दिता अत एव उत्कण्ठा ये नीलकण्ठाः तेषां कलाः केकाः तासामनुबन्धोस्यास्तीति** which was closely followed by the notes of the peacocks &c.

 **आश्वास्यादौ** &c — **आश्वास्यैव** Megh. II. 52 **आज्ञातन्तु** &c.— For the idea cf. Mg. I. 10— **आशाबन्धः कुसुमसदृशं प्रायशो ह्यङ्गनानां सद्यःपाति प्रणमि हृदयं विप्रयोगे रुणाद्धि।**

 P. 189. **उन्मादो**०**— उन्माद एव उपरागः।** See Jag.; **उपरागस्तु पुंसि स्याद्राहुमासेकेचन्द्रयोः। नवेषु लोध्रप्रसवेषु** &c.—cf. Megh. II. 43; again— **श्यामास्वङ्गं चकितहरिणीप्रेक्षणे दृष्टिपातं वक्त्रच्छायां शशिनि शिखिनो बर्हभारेषु केशान्। वत्पश्यामि प्रतमुषु नदीवीचिषु भ्रूविलासान्** &c; and for a similar idea Rag VIII. 59. Fig. **विशेषालं. **

 **प्रियजन—** &c.— **प्रियजनविरहेण य आधिः** mental pain or anguish **स एव व्याधिः तस्य बेर्गः व्याधिः** may also be taken in its usual sense of bodily pain or torment. See trans. The fig in this sl, is **परिकर.**

 ** सुलभानुकारः—सुलभः अनुकारः पत्र। निर्माणसन्निवेशः—** The arrangement of creation, i. e. the manner in which created things are presented to view, The poet often uses the word **निर्माण**. in the sense of a created thing. See Jag.; also IX. 50.

 P. 190. **भवद्धिः—**&c—The address here and in the following Slokas to the animals of the forest is an obvious imitation of Kali.'s Vik. IV.

 **सवाङ्ङ्गप्रकृतिº— सर्वेषु अङ्गेषु प्रकृत्वा रमणीया, प्रगल्भ॰**—i. e . just in budding youth, Lit. in an age when the operation of love within is very strong and its external manifestations charming on account of their very imperfectness. Cf. for the idea **मुग्धत्वस्य च यौवनस्य च सखे मध्ये मधुश्रीः स्थिता। ** Vik. II. 7.

 **ध्रुवमनवलर॰— म प्रशन्तः (युक्तः) अवसरः अनवसरः तेन ग्रस्तः।** Every one, acting under the influence of love, is too much busy with his own affairs to attend to me and so my petition is ill—timed Fig **अर्थान्तरन्यास.**

 **कान्तदन्सं—० दन्तमाल (रञ्जिता दन्तमाला यस्य)** V. I is better, as **कान्त** is ot appropriate with the teeth of a monkey. **काम्पिल्लक॰—** Better read **गण्डपालि** as a separate epithet of **वक्त्र; प्रसववत् प्रसवेन वा पाटला गण्डपाली पत्र तत्‌० दन्तमालं, गण्डपालि च अत एव पाका॰.** The reddened teeth looked like the seeds of the pomegranate while the temple-region and the lips, parted asuder, like its opened rind. If we take **पालिवा॰** as one word the comp. will have to be explained as **गण्डपालि अतएव पाकारुण** &c. But **गण्डपालि** alone does not bear out the comparison to a ripened pomegranate. The two epithets must be taken together to make the comparison proper. Fig. Nidars'aná.

 P. 191. **प्रियतमास्कन्ध॰— एष नीपस्कन्धनिषण्णहस्तः नागराजस्तिष्ठति।** Vik. IV. **स्थिति—l**ivelihood; is giving her food. **परिचयप्रागल्भ्यं— परिचयेन यत्प्रगल्भ्यं तत्** boldness brought on by familiarity. प्रागस्थय प्रगल्भब्यापार. Fig; Svabhavokti. **भावर्जित—**drawn together, collected. **ज्यानि—**ths state of being old: hence loss, deprivation; fr. **ज्या+ नि; ग्लाङ्खाज्याहाम्यो निः** ७० **ग्लानि, हानि** ६०. **व्यासङ्ग—** may also mean **विगतः आसङ्गः** their (of the bees) atsending to something else. As the bees came there but found not the rut, they silently left the elephant.** मूनं—**&c. The fig. is **अनुमान स्तम्बेरमः— स्तम्ने** (a clump of grass or a shrub) **रमते असौ. **

 P. 192. **प्रत्यय॰— प्रत्यग्रं विकसितः यः कदम्बसङ्घातः** (bunches of the Kad. flowers) **तस्य सुभिशीतलामोदेन बहकं संवलितः यः... निष्यन्दः तेन कर्दमितं (कईमोस्य सञ्जातः) च तत्कषायं च।** Here the Kad, trees are supposed to be on the bank of the lake. We shuold rather have read **सङ्गलित** for **संवलित** which improves the sense. Explain **•सङ्घातवत् सुगमः शीतलश्च आमोदः यस्य तादृक् श्व बहुलं यथा तथा सङ्गलितः यः** &c. **तेन कर्दमितं ६० कर्दमिततीर—** V. 1.— here **तीर** seems to be a mislection for **नीर.** Jag's reading is०**करेम्मितकरटः** but we have rejected this because when Madh. sees the elephant the latter was in the water so that he could not have been **कर्दमितकरट** as the rut must have been washed off. **उदलित** &c and **अनवरत** &c. may be taken as adv.s or adj s qualifying **सरः; समुद्दलितानि यानि कमलिनीखण्डानि तेभ्यः प्रकीणैः पर्णानां कोमलाङ्कुराणां निकरः यस्मिन्, or यस्मिन्कर्मणि तद्यथा तथा।** translating we have followed the reading **प्रकीर्णकेसरमृणाल** &c. see foot—note. **अनवरतं प्रवृत्तं धत्कमनीयं कर्णतालताण्डवं** (the harmonious and regular play flapping—of the ears) **तेन प्रचलाः तरङ्गास्तेभ्यो वितता ये नीहारास्तेभ्यो वित्रस्ताः कुररसारसा यस्मिन् or यस्मिन् कर्माण तथा। ताल** is properly the marking of musical intervals by striking together the hands; hence any regular motion as that of the ears here. The use of the word **कमनीय** shows that the fispping of the ess was regular. The elephant was enjoying the bath and so was moving his ears regularly. For the use of **कर्णताल** of. Rag. VII. 39 **विस्तारितः कुञ्जरकर्णतालैः &c **

 ** कान्तानुवृत्ति ०—** This expression and the following sl. with the substitution of **यद्** for **न** in the last line occur in the Uttar. (111. 16). **कान्तायाः अनुवृत्तिः तत्र चातुर्यम्**

 ** कीलो॰— लीलया उत्खाताः** rooted up **मृणालकाण्डा एव, तेषां वा, कवलास्तेषां छेदेषु** at the end of. **पुष्यत्—**developing, blooming. **गण्डून** &.— of. **ददो रसात्पङ्कजरेणगग्धि गजाय गण्डूषजलं करेणुः।** Kum. III. 37, where it is the female that humours the male. **काम**—This is properly used as here when one gives one's consent or expresses one's approval with something to find fault with (अक **नानुमतौ कामम्** Amara); so it means—I grant all this and yet. **भनराल॰— न भरालमनरालं नालं यस्य तादृं नलिनीपत्रनेवातपत्रम्।**

 ** चिगुच्छ्वासित** &c.— **उध्छ्वसितमेव वैशसं;** lit, the calamity in the shape of life. **वैशस** properly—destruction or killing; hence also what causes destruction of mental case, distress, calainity.

 P. 193. **उन्माद ०— अन्तरित** separated from.**व्यञ्जकं**— **व्यमक्तीति** what manifests, something that awakens or oulls up a past impression, an excitant of a feeling. **सहज **ⅰ. e. not brought about by any external means **जीविताशा ०— जीविताशायां व्यसने** (persis. tence in) a persistent or strong desire for life. **परिच्छेद—** final conclusion. Sce I. 21. p. 34

 ** आवद्ध॰—** Adv. **आवशः वेपथुः यस्मिन्कर्मणि तथा तथा विनापि—** Because **अतिस्नेहः पापशङ्की** as Kali, says; or **प्रेम पश्यति भयान्यपदेपि।** Kir. 1X 70. **तस्सर्वमेकपदे **&c.— Because he had now steeled his heart against the worst that might come to pass,

 P. 194, **तथाविधं –i . e **. on whose account I always appre. hended misfortunes and so had my heart always full of feverish anxiety,

 **वज्रक्रीलं— वज्रस्य कील इव **ⅰ. e. hard to break. **स्वत्प्रायाणे—** He does not say **मरणे;** the very idea is horrid to him.

 **तत्किं व खलु** &c—Madh, was yet in a trance which might end in death, and so he wants to die before life had left Madhava.

 P. 195. **उल्लसित॰— उल्लसितः विस्मयः** **यासु** in which there arose wonder (at the beauty). **निपीतवत्यः—** The idea is peculiar to Sans ; **नेत्राभ्यां पा** means to look at or gaze on intently or longingly, or with eyes rivetted on the object of sight. See Rag. II. 19. JII. 17 &c. Megh 1. 16. &c. **नवप्रणय॰— नवेन प्रणयेन ये विभ्रमाः** sportive gestures, dalliance : &c.

 **अचरमे वयसि** &c.— Cf. **यत्कल्याणं वयसि तरुणे भाजनं तस्य जातः।** Uttar.

 **आपूर्णश्च** &c— **च यातः च**— the two as indicate the simultaneous— nest of the two acts. The moment the moon attained fulness she fell into the mouth of Rahu, &c. **फलेग्रहिः—** see Jag.; formed irregularly; **फलेग्रहिरात्मम्भरिश्च। ** Pán. III. 2. 26. The figures of speech in the al, are **समुच्चय** and **दृष्टान्त.**

 **मालतीº— स्वयङ्ग्राहेण जीवितेश्वरः स्वयं॰ मालत्याः स्वर्यग्राहº अपश्चिमः— नास्ति पश्चिमो यस्मात्** to which there is no other succeeding i, e. the last one. It is thus equivalent to **पश्चिमः** c.f **अनुत्तम (निचैन दुब्यमामुरनुत्तमं,)** And **अनुत्तर अनुत्तरराणि विलसितानि** D K.). **अपश्चिम** often occurs in plays **अर्थ पाश्वमः (अपश्चिमः** v. 1.) **तै रामस्य शिरसि पाइपङ्कजस्पर्शः** Uttar I.p 47: see A Dio

 P. 196. **भवति आपगे—** Of course he addresses the presiding deity of the river,

 **योगिन्यस्मि—** This she says to inspire confidence in him. **अत्याहितं—** see p. 81.

 **अनपेक्षितास्मरत्रस्थः—** What Madh means is that the wind should not have brought him back to consciousness and made him experience the pain of separation again.

 P. 197. **भगवन्** &c—Cf. the similar address to the Southern breeze in Vık. 11. 20.

 **अखिलज तु॰**—Cf. **जगत्प्राणसमीरणाः**। Amara, **मातरिश्चन्— मातरि अन्तरिक्ष श्वयति सञ्चरतीति।** This word occurs in the Veda and is thus derived by Yâkoa— **मातरिश्वा वायुमतिर्यन्तरिक्षे श्वसिति मातर्याशु अनिति वा।**

 **विकसत्** &c** **—**विकपन्ति यात्रि कदम्बानि तेषां निकुरज्वस्तस्य पांसुना। जीवितं वह—** He means—Do nos restore life to my body but bear it, along with the pollen of flowers, to where &c. Of. for a similar request **डासानय प्रीयमतां मम वा समीपं मां वा नयाशु कलभाषिणि पत्र कान्ता॥** Vik. 1V. 11.

** एते** &c.— (See foot—note), **सुन** a flower. **पौर॰— ०अङ्गमार्या ध्यक्षलेका अलका वलये इन** (oreeper—like i, e. long and flowing) **अककनलः हाल कुठने तन्याजेनोपभुक्तमानने वेः। शनिद्र**—blooming. **व्यु**—a swarm of. Cons.— **वर्षानिकाः विरहिणः कर्षन्ति**। In the trans. of this sl. the words— borment those in separatiou—are accidentally omitted.

 P. 198. **प्रियतमा॰— स्तनयोः उन्नाहः स्तनोन्नाषः** (ⅰ.e** उन्नतस्तनौ) तेन दुर्ललिता मूर्तिः यस्याः;** which was affectionately worn on. **दुर्ललित— दुष्टुं ललितं यस्य** one fondled too much, treated with too much affection.

 **सुग्न्धेन्दु** &०.—**अवलोकहेल**या (sport, pleasure) **विशृङ्खलं** (lit unrestrained, hence excessive) **यत्कुतूहलं तस्य निह्नवाय** i. e. as I tried to conceal the agitation of my heart by appearing to weave the wreath. **दुन्येस्त—**not only were the flowers not properly put in or arranged but the weaving was also faulty.

 P. 199. **स्वराप्रस्तावः— स्वरायाः प्रस्तावः। प्रियाप्रणयिनी— प्रियायाः प्रणयोस्या अस्तीति। देहोराहº— देहोद्दाह एव व्यसनं (**an evil, a calamity) **तेन गुरवः**, or better still **देहोदाहे यद्वसनं** **तेन गुरवः** agonising because of their persistence in burning the body. **प्रगुणं— प्रकृष्ठो गुणो यस्य** (adj.). **यस्मिन् कर्मणि वा** (adv.).

 P. 200. **गाढानुराग॰—**i.e which indicated strong love. **तदा तदा** on various occasions and hence the pl. **गतागतानि** and not as Jag. has it; see com. **स्नेहाकराणि** the mines i, e. abodes of or birth—place of affection as they deepened it more and more every time. **करवाल—**a sword (also **करपाल);** **करः बालः** (fr. **बल् वेष्टने)** **यस्य, करेण वल्यते वा.**

 P. 201. **रामणीयक॰— रामणीयकं** (see I. 21) **एव गुणः तदर्थम्.** **सुकृतं—** that happy combination. **अस्तु—** should last for the full time. **अकाल—** Because in autumn the sky is usually quite free from clouds (and hence **शरदिन्दुच॰** which is very bright) and any sudden appearance of clouds is untimely. The fig. in this sl. is **अप्रस्तुतप्रशंसा.**

** उत्पात— केतुकवकिता** Jag.; **धूमलेखा** rather means the tail of a comet, whose appearance is sudden and unexpected. Fig. Upamá,

 **निर्माण** is used here (as in other places by the poet) in the sense of-a created form. **हि** is here **अवधारणार्थे** (to be sure; decidedly). Her very form is so lovely that for its sake (if not for any other consideration) she ought certainly to be treated tenderly or with feelings of awe, For, **आकृतिविशेषेष्वादरः पदं करोति।**

 P. 202. **नैसर्गिकी— निसर्गेच निर्वृत्ता** lit, brought about or fixed by nature, natural. These two lines occur in the Uttar. (see. 1. 14). **न सुसलैः**—Jag. reads **चरणैः** and this reading at first sight appears better as contrasted with **मूर्धन्.** But the point here is to show the extreme incongruity of the two acts, the idea beings thing which ought to be treated but gently should not be used with extreme violence. This is strikingly brought out by the use of **मुसल**, the blow given by which is instanta— neously crushing.

 **परिपन्थिनी—परि दोषाख्यार्न पन्थयितुं** to proclaim **शीलमस्याः** lit. one given to finding fault with another, hence an enemy.

 **गुरुचर्या**—is **गुरुसेवा** attendance upon and service done to a Guru. This is of primary importance to a religious student. Without Gurubhakti proper success can never be attained in religions practices. **अभियोग—** close application. **आक्षेपिणी सिद्धि —** is the power to bear one aloft and then through space.

 **व्यतिकर इव** &c.—This line occurs in Uttar. (V. 13.) **तामसः वैद्युतश्च—**Jag. understands the **व्यतिकर** in a metaphorical sense. But Mak.'s words **आश्चर्यमाश्चर्यं** show that the darkness and th lightning—like flash of light were real. Sau, as she flew into the sky, created these by her miraculous power that Mak. might not at once see what was going to happen.

 P. 203. **किमयमर्थो** &c.— See Jag.; Mak does not know why Sau. should have carried away Madh. He has his own mis-givings. Perhaps Kapal., wishing to wreak her vengeance on Madh, might have also come in disguise with the Bakula wreath and managed to carry away Madh. In this case his worst fears might be realised and the affair might thus prove to be a calamity. This is what Jag. means by **कपालकुण्डलानयमे** &c.

 **अस्तोकविस्मयं—** Wonder at the miraculous power displayed by Saud. in creating a mixture of light and darkness, **अपस्मृत—** Sau's appearance and the wonderful feat performed by her made Mak. quite forget for a time the past occurrences. **अविस्मृत,** the reading of the N. Ed., will not do, as it leaves no room for joy (as the **पूर्ववृत्त** was not forgotten). **नूतनभय—** on account of the uncertainty that hung over Madh's fate, The rhetorical fig. in this sl. is Kavyalinga.

 P. 201. **प्रतिमुहूर्त— प्रतिमुहूर्त (मुहूर्ते मुहूर्ते) विशेषरम्याणि चाटूनि**— sweet speeches or lispings.

** अनियत॰— अनियत** not restricted or dne to any cause; see Jag. **विराजत्** &०—**विराजन्तः कतिपये कोमलदन्ता एव कुड्मलाग्राणि यस्य। स्मरामि**— I remember with sorrow **(उत्कण्ठापूर्वकं स्मरामि**) We should have: expected the Gen in this sense. **अत्र अनियतरुदितस्मितं स्खलदसमञ्जसमिति विशेषणानुगुण्याद्वदनकमलकमित्यत्र परिणामालङ्कारः। केवलकमलस्य प्रकृतक्रियान्वयित्वानुपपत्तेः। परिणामक्रियार्थश्चेद्विषयी विषयात्मना। इति लक्षणात्। दन्तकुड्मलाग्रमित्यत्रापि क्रियान्वयविवक्षाय परिणामो रूपकं वा।** Virarâghava on Uttar. IV. 4.

 P. 206 **प्रगुणीकृतानि— **nourished, caused to be developed; **प्रकृष्टो गुणः** (excellence due to proper nourishment) **येषां तथा सम्पद्यमानानि कृतानि।**

** दन्तपाञ्चालिकेव—**The simile implies that Kám. did all this with that tenderness of heart with which children fondle and caress their dolls. **विनय—**training, education.

** अकारण॰—अकारणं स्मेरमतएव मनोहरमाननं यस्य। गौरसर्षपः—** It was customary to apply the powder of white mustard to the forehead and the top of the head of a new born child to keep off evil influences (and probably also to prevent the child from catching cold); cf. **०तालुनि विन्यस्तगौरसर्षपोन्मिश्रभूतिलेशः** ..**पुत्रकः** &c.Kâd. **स्तनन्धयः—स्तनं धयतीति।**

 P. 207. **अवधूय—** Having shaken ie throw myself off. उत्क**ण्ठावेगा**— Jag.'s explanation of this as—**जन्मान्तरेपि** &c doan not seem to be correct, as such an idea is precluded by the following al; so this means the force i, e. intensity of anguish.

 **सङ्गमः कर्मणां भेदात्** &c— Here the poet probably follows Bana—Cf. **अन्यामेव स्वकर्मफलपरिपाकोपचितामसाववशो नीयते भूमिमसावप्यात्मघातिनः केवलमेनसा संयुज्यते। अत्र विचार्यमाणे स्वार्थ एव प्राणपरित्यागोयमसह्यशोकवेदना प्रतीकारत्वादात्मनः।** Kád. p. 136. For the idea of the dead meeting in heaven, cf.—

"And father cardinal, I have heard you say  
That we shall see and know our friends in heaven:  
If that be true, I shall see my boy again;"

Shakespeare, King John Act III Sce. 4.

 P. 208. **मधुमतीस्रोतः** &c— **मधुमतीस्त्रोतसा सन्दानित** (encircled, begirt) **अत एव पवित्रा मेखला यस्य,**

 ** सम्भवं—**& pressing crowd.

 P. 209 **सुवर्णविन्दु—**. 6. that part of the mountain where the Linga of Siva called Suvarnabindu (see p. 77) was situated,

 **झटिति—**&—The sudden and wonderful appearance of Madh. was reassuring to the party and Mad. aud Lav. naturally expected to see Mål. also. Hence their remark.

**दिष्ट्या **&c.**—** Kâm. and Mak. were just going to express their satisfaction it Madh.'s sight, and exclaimed **दिष्ट्या** &c; but before they could finish their speech, they heard the voice of some one announcing how Bhūrivasu, unable to ear the pang of separation from Mâl, was advancing to Suvarnabindu, resolved upon puting an end to his existence and so suddenly broke out into **हा कष्टं** &c.

 **असिपत्र—** may mean the blade of a sword, or a very thin short sword with a broad blade **(असिपत्रमिव).** **०पत्राणां ०छटायाश्चासारो ययोः **&c. The fig is **अतिशयोक्ति.**

 **अनुकुरुते—** same time. Fate is acting favourably and cruelly at the

 ** समस्तलोकान्तराल—** Jag. reads **लोकालो कान्तराल—** which rather means the space encircled by the mountain Lokaloka, for which see Dr. Bhandarkar's notes or Apte's Dic. or our notes on Rag. 1. 68. **मङ्गलº** — **मङ्गलार्थः प्रदीपः मङ्गलप्रदीपः** **तया भूपः** (A comp सुन्पा) तम्.

 P. 210. **जन्मान्तरादिव—**Here **इव** indicates an Utpreksha. **उपराप इव** is an Upamà. **अनर्थः**— in the shape of Bhûrivasu's impending death. **अन्यथा—** on account of a different cause. **को माम** &o.—
These two lines form the latter part of Uttar. VII. 4 also. fuger**—पाकाभिमुखस्य– **here the **पाक** means destruction of Mâl. in any way. Fig. Arthantaranyàsa. Cf. **अथवा भवितव्यानां द्वाराणि भवन्ति सर्वत्र।** S'ak. I. 15. For an opposite function discharged by fate cf **दीपादन्यस्मादपि मध्यादपि जलनिधेर्दिशोप्यन्तात्। आनीय झटिति घटयति विधिरभिमतमभिमुखीभूतः॥** Rat I. 6.

 **श्रीपर्वतात्** &c.— **तयैव सह**— Jag. is wrong in saying **मालत्या सहः** it should be **तथा योगिन्या सह. अनन्तरं—अन्तरिता** V. i.— who disappeared after. Saud., it will be seen, on hearing of the immediate peril in which Bhù. stood, hastened to avert the catastrophe by telling him about Màl.'s safe arrival there. Madh. evidently could not account for her sudden disappearance.

 P. 211 **चिरनिरुद्धº—चिरनिरुद्धः** choked **यः निश्वासः तेन निश्चलम्.**

 **अम्बुनिवह—**The shower was of course caused by Sau. to refresh Màl. and others.

 ** वितत॰—** Jag reads **विततश्वासा नासा;** her nose has the breath flowing through it again.**प्रसन्न** for **प्रणुन्न,** however, has no propriety. **ºसोन्नाहेन प्रणुन्नौ** (heaved up or set in motion) **पयोधरौ यत्र।** The fig, in the first three lines is and in the last Upamâ. The simile is a happy one here; cf. Vik. I. 5. **(महोत्पलं प्रत्युषसीव पद्मिनी)** 6 and 7.

 P. 212 **अग्निचये–**i.e** ** the mass of flames rising up.**गुरु॰—गुरु सम्मदः** joy **विस्मयश्च यस्य.**

 **वागमृत—** Her words were more cooling (comforting) than the phys cal shower as they at once removed their anxiety on account of Buúrivasu.

 **जीवय** &c.— Because the life of all deperdel on that of Mâl.

 **तुहिन॰—तुहिनसङ्गवत् शील्लैः **cooling like the contact of snow (allaying mental fever) also.

 ** मनोरथा॰— मनोरथमतिक्रान्तं दर्शनं यस्याः** lit., the idea of seeing whom was not to be entertained even in thought.

 P. 213. **कपाल॰—**see Jag: **तस्माज्जनिता आपद् येन तस्मात्। निर्वन्ध—** presistent effort, perseverance.

 **विजृम्भित—** result, outcome (also the expansion of the story— Perhaps here the poet gives his justification for adding the last opr Acts).

 **पुनरुक्तo— (पुनरुक्तमिव)** **पुनरुक्तं दारुणं यस्य** which repeated its cruelty (Mâl.being twice in imminent risk of life).

** सत्सर्व&c.—**Why she exerted herself so much and saved the lives of all-all this is now explained.

** P. 214.स्पृहणीसिध्दिः—**Siddhi—such miraculous power acquired by the practice of Yoga as enabled her to produce light and darkness, to cause a shower of rainwater to fall down &c. **एवंविधैः विलसितैः**-Acts like these-your rescuing Màl. from the jaws of death and exertions to save the lives of so many other persons &c. This is an additional reason why she is azar.**बन्धा.अतिबोधिसत्त्वैः—बोधिसत्त्वान् अतिक्रान्तानि तैः** A prep. Tat. comp; which out do those of the Bodhisatvas. Bodhisatva[^1346] for his essence; i. e. he is a being who through all his bodily existences is destined in some final existence to become a Buddha, M. W. For other particulars see M. W.'s Buddhism, p. p. 98, 180, kc,")" (from **बोधि** knowledge) is a particular rank in Bhuddhistic Sainthood, attainable by the performance of virtuous and pious acts through a series of births and leading to the attainment of the rank of a supreme Budha. The performance of benevolent deeds, even at the risk of one's life, is a characteristic of the Bodhisatvas, Honge Kâm.'s remark. **उद्भूत** &c**.—उद्भूतानि भूरीणि फलानि तैः शालते तत्।**

[^1346]: # "A Bodhisatva is one who has knowledge (derived from selfenlightening indellect

** भगवतीसम्बन्ध—भगवतीसम्बन्धेन (अस्मासु) पक्षपासिन्या. भगवती॰—भगवत्या स्नेहः तस्मान्निर्गतः विशेषः यस्मिन्कर्माणि तद्यथा तथा।**

** P. 215.अपि &c.—चिन्ता** i. e . one must express a desire and then can the Chintamani grant it. **इदं त्वo**—The fig. here is**व्यतिरेक** For a similar idea comp. Sâk. VII. 30. **प्रथमानुराग॰— प्रथमम् अनुरागेण घटिता।**

** P. 216.कार्यनिधाने—**The store i. e. the prime cause of the successful issue of events.

** महाद्भूतं प्रकरणम्—**Here although by Prakarna the poet apparently means 'an affair, a course of events', he, in his ecstasy of joy, doubtless pronounces his judgment on his own performance, which is a Prakarna technically so called.

** इतरेतराo—इतरेतरापत्ययोः सम्बन्ध आत्मा यस्य.** Here **आत्मा** may mean **स्वरुप**, or the essential part.**वस्तुवृतं**—Jag. takes these as two words; as one word it means the happening of events **(वस्तुनो वृत्तम्)—**Bhû, had not only never signified his wish to bestow Mal. on Mádh., but had actually given her away to Nandans,

** P. 217. नन्दनोपग्रहात्—**Here **उपग्रह** may mean ‛conciliation, favourableness' (cf.**सोपग्रहं** Kád. p. p. 118, 203.) or the malicious planet (in the shape of Nandana)**श्रावकावस्थायां—श्रावक** is used here in the sense of ‛a pupil.'

** प्रधानप्रकृतिकोपः—कोप—**displeasure. There is some difficulty here as to the meaning to be assigned to **प्रधानप्रकृति, प्रकृति** doubtless means here ‘a minister' and so it can refer to Nandan who was the King's **नर्मसचिव** (a kind of minister). But as he was not the chief minister, we take **प्रधान** to mean 'the king' or the chief person in the kingdom, and so this means **प्रधानपकृत्योः कोपं** the displeasure of the king and his minister; if taken in this sense all difficulty vanishes. This seems to be the poet's meaning at least as that was the final object of Kâm., and that was attained, as shown by her words at **तां याचते नरपतेर्नर्मसुहृन् नन्दनो नृपमुखेन। तत्साक्षात्प्रतिषेधः कोपाय शिवस्वयमुपायः॥** I. 11. Dr. Bhândurkar however, who does not take प्रधान in the sense of the king' is at some pains to assign a meaning to the words and wishing to sift the question thoroughly enters into a long discussion of the term **प्रकृति** (of course to the benefit of the student). Seehis notes.

** संस्तुतापलापिण्यः—महतां—**great by their displomacy, consummate politicians.**संस्कृतं** (lit. what is familiar to the mind, the subject of constant thought, the object in view अपलपन्ति (lit, to talk) away, conceal) **इति.**

** पुण्यैः —** our collective merit; or by your merit. **उपक्रमैः**—plans, schemes or devices.**निष्णातः**—skilfully brought about (adj. to **समा**o);or as Jag. takes it (see trans).

** P. 218.तथापीदमस्तु—**This is what is technically called the Bharatavákya. See Intro. p. 4.

 **सन्तः—** See trans; or the cons may be **सुकृतिनः सन्तः विध्वस्तपायोदयाः सन्तु।** **घनबन्धु॰ — घना या बन्धूनां** (near relatives) **बान्धवानां**— (kinsmen) **च** &c.—**गोष्ठी तत्र प्रमोदः यासाम्।**

**APPENDIX.  
1**

**FIGURES OF SPEECH MENTIONED IN THE**

**COMMENTARY OR NOTES[^1347]**

[^1347]: # "The definitions are taken from the K. P. Only the important figures are noticed here."

** अतिशयोक्ति—**or Hyperbole is of tour kinds of which one of frequent occurrence is **प्रस्तुतस्य यदन्यत्वं— सातिशयोक्तिर्विज्ञेया;** i.e. when the thing in hand is described as of a different kind (superior in excellence or beauty) that is Atis'ayokti.

** अनुप्रास—**or Alliteration is the repetition of similar letters, syllables or sounds.

** अनुमान—**or Inference is defined as अनुमानं **तदुक्तं यत्साध्यसाध**; i.e. the (poetical) expression of a (logical) Reason and a Conclusion.

** अपह्नुति —प्रकृतं यन्निषिध्यान्यत्साध्यते सा त्वपह्नुतिः**— That is Apahnuti in which the matter in hand (i, e. the **उपमेय**) is denied or shown to be unreal and another (i. e. the उपमान) is established as real (or is superimposed upon it).

** अप्रस्तुतप्रशंसा—अप्रस्तुतप्रशंसा सा या सैव प्रस्तुताश्रया**— the description of what is not the matter in hand implying the matter in hand, It is of five kinds: **कार्ये निमित्ते सामान्ये विशेषे प्रस्तुते सति। तदन्यस्य वचस्तुल्ये तुल्यस्येति च पञ्चधा**॥ i. e. when the matter in hand is (1) an effect, information about which is conveyed by stating the cause; (2) a cause implied by the statement of the effect; (3) a general assertion by stating a particular instance; (4) a particular instance by stating a general assertion; and (5) a similar thing implied by what resembles it.

** अर्थान्तरन्यास—**Or Corroboration; **'सामान्यं वा विशेषो वा तदन्येन समर्थ्यते। यत्र सोर्थान्तरन्यासः साधर्म्येणेतरेण वा॥** Where a general proposition is adduced to support a particular instance, or a particular instance to support a general proposition, either under a resemblance or a contrast, that is Artha'ntaranya'sa.

** आक्षेप—**(Cf. Greek 'Paraleipsis) **निषेधो वक्तुमिष्टस्य यो विशेषाभिधित्सया। वक्षमाणोक्तविषयः स आक्षेपः।** That is A kshspa in which something really intended to be said (i.e. the matter in hand) is apparently suppressed or denied with a view to convey a particular meaning. Vâmana defines this as "**उपमानाक्षेपश्वाक्षेप**"g which is identical with Mammata's Pratipa.

** उत्प्रेक्षा—**or Poetical Probability: **सम्भावनमथोत्प्रेक्षा प्रकृतस्य समेन यत्। प्रकृतमात्मनः समं करोतीति सममुपमानम्।** Apprehending the objeot under consideration as looking identical with something to which it is compared is what is termed utpreksha'. It is of two kinds (1) expressed or (2) understood. The expressed is one wherein such words as ध्रुवं मन्ये &c. are used: the understood is one in which such words are not used. It is again of three kinds, **हेतूत्प्रेक्षा, फलोत्प्रेक्षा** and **वस्तुत्प्रेक्षा** or **स्वरूपोत्प्रेक्षा.**

** उपमा—**or Comparison —**साधर्म्यमुपमा भेदे, पूर्णा लुप्ता च साऽग्रिमा। श्रौत्यार्थी च भवेद्वाक्ये समासे तद्धिते तथा**॥ The (striking) possession of a common property, when there is difference, is Upama'.

** उपमान—**means **सधारणधर्मत्त्वेन प्रसिद्धः पदार्थः** as कमल in the instance **कमलमिव मुखं मनोज्ञम्;** here **मनोज्ञत्व** is the **साधारणधर्म** and **कमल** is well known to possess this. **उपमेय** is **साधारणधर्मवत्त्वेन वर्णनीयः पदार्थः** as **मुख** in the given example. **साधर्म्य** is explained as **समानः धर्मः ययोः (उपमानोपमेययोः) तौ सधर्माणौ तयाोर्भावः साधर्म्यम्। समान = तुल्य** may also mean **एक** in some cases. **भेदे** means when the **उपमान** and **उपमेय** are two different things and not the same. **उपमान** or the thing compared to, **उपमेय** or the thing compared, **साधारणधर्म** or the common property, and the **उपमानप्रातपादकशब्द** or words conveying the sense of comparison such as य**था, इव, तुल्य, सदृश** &c. are the four constituents of **उपमा** . When all these four are present, the Upama' is called gaf or complete, and when one or two or three of these four are dropped the Upama is **लुप्ता** or Elliptical. The former (i, e f is of two kinds:—(1)**श्रौती** in which such words **यथा इव** &c. (i, e̟, the **धर्मवाचक** words) are used; or the aff **वत्** in the sons of **इव** by ' **तत्र तस्येव**' Pán V. 1. 116. is employed; (2) and **आर्थी** in which such words as **तुल्य, सदृश** &c. (i. e. the**धर्मिवाचक** words) are used, or the aff. **वत्** is used in the sense of **तुल्य** by ' तेन तुल्यं &c. Pân V. I 115.

 Mammatá mentions in all 25 varieties of Upama' but they are not given here as of little use to junior students.

** काव्यलिङ्ग—**or the poetical Reason; **काव्यलिङ्गं हेतोर्वाक्यपदार्थता।** Ka'vyalinga is the statement of a reason in the form of (1) a sentence, or (2) of a word or (3) words. Or to make the definition simpler **वाक्यपदार्थयोः हेतुता**—that is **काव्य॰** wherein either & sentence or a word (or words) is intended to give a reason for the statement made in the whole sentence. The **हेतु** according to some must be **आर्थ** or implied.

** दीपक—(कारक)—कारकस्य च बह्वीषु क्रियासु सुकृद्वृत्तिः दीपकम्**॥ When a casenoun occurring once is connected with a plurality of verbs that is (the second kind of) **दीपक**.

** दृष्टान्त—दृष्टान्तः पुनरेतेषां सर्वेषां प्रतिबिम्बनम्**। Illustration by an example is when all these (i. e. the common property, the उपमेय and the उपमान) are reflectively represented.

** निदर्शना—निदर्शना। अभवन्वस्तुसम्बन्ध उपमापरिकल्पकः॥** When an (apparently) impossible connection of things implies a comparison that is called **निदर्शना** **निदर्शनं दृष्टान्तकरणं** (citing an instan 00) **यथाश्रुतमात्रेणासम्भवी वस्तुसम्बन्धः (वस्तुनोर्वाक्यार्थयोः पदार्थयोर्वा सम्बन्धः अन्वयः) यत्रोपमां कल्पयित्वा पर्यवस्यति सैका निदर्शना। सा च द्विधा अवान्तरवाक्यभेदे तदभेदे च। Pradîpa. 'स्वस्वहेत्वन्वयस्योक्तिः क्रिययैव च साऽपरा। यत्र क्रिययैव स्वस्य स्वहेतोश्वान्वयो हेतुहेतुमद्भावरूपः ख्याप्यते साऽपरा निदर्शना**—where by an action itself is indicated its own connection with its cause (that of cause and effect) that is the second kind of Nidars'ana'.

** परिकर—विशेषणैर्यत्साकूतैरुक्तिः परिकरस्तु सः। साकूतैः साभिप्रायैः। उक्तिरर्थाद्विशेषस्य।** That is Parikara where there is a description (of course of the subject) with attributes which are significant i. have an implied meaning **(व्यङ्ग्य).** Here **विशेषण** and **विशेष्य** are dependent on each other. In Ká'vyalinga, कार्यकारणभाव is necessary; so there is no **व्यङ्ग्य.** But परिकर contains the व्यङ्ग्य which produces the charm. According to Jagannátha, the use of even one significant adjective is sufficient for Parikara.

** पर्यायोक्त—पर्यायोक्तं** **विना वाच्यवाचकत्वेन यद्वचः।** That figure of speech is known as Parya'yokta wherein we have the statement of a fact without the relation of **वाच्य** (the expressed) and वाचक (the expresser) between that fact and the words which bring it out. This fig. corresponds to 'Periphrasis.

** भ्रान्तिमान् — भ्रान्तिमानन्यसंवित्तत्तुल्यदर्शने।'** When on seeing a thing (tho **प्राकरणिक** one) the knowledge of another thing (the **अप्राकरणिक** one) similar to it is attained, that is termed Bhra'ntima'n. In other words when the **अप्राकरणिक** thing is mistaken for the **प्राकरणिक**, the figure is **भ्रान्तिमान्.**

** यथासङ्ख्य—यथासङ्ख्यं क्रमेणैव क्रमिकाणां समन्वयः।** That is the connection in the same order, of objects, successively metioned.

** रूपक or Metaphor —** **तद्रूपकमभेदो य उपमानोपमेययोः।** The identity of **उपमान** and the **उपमेय** is Rupaka. When two things known to be different from each other, still to show their great resemblance, are identified together, the fig. is Ru'paka. Hence it is plain that in a Rapaka the **उपमेय** and the **उपमान** (the **प्रकृत** and the**अप्रकृत**) must be mentioned in words.

** विरोध—विरोधः सोऽविरुद्धेपि विरुद्धत्वेन यद्वचः।** When two things are represented as incongruous, when really there is no incongruity between them, that is Virodha or Antithesis (also called **विरोधाभास** or Semblance of incongruity).

** विशेष—विना प्रसिद्धमाधारमाधेयस्य व्यवस्थितिः।** When an object is represented as abiding outside its proper abode, it is Vis'esha.

** विषम—**That is Vishama in which some unusual or incompatible relation between cause and effect is described.

** व्यतिरेक—उपमानाद्यदन्यस्य व्यतिरेकः स एव सः।** a figure of speech which consists in representing the Upameya as superior to the Upama'na in some particular respect.

** श्लेष—**Pun, double entendre, the susceptibility of a word or words to yield two or more meanings.

** सम—समं योग्यतया योगो यदि सम्भावितः क्वचित्।** The fig. सम occurs when there is an ascertainment of a connection as fit between two things, both (1) superior or (2) inferior.

** समुच्चय—। सतत्सिद्धिहेतावेकस्मिन्यन्नान्यत्तत्करं भवेत् मुच्चयोसौ**' when one cause of the producing of an effect, is present and yet others are mentioned as producing the same effect, that is Samuchchaya.

** सार—उत्तरोत्तरमुत्कर्षो भवेत्सारः परावधिः।** When an excellence goes on rising, until a culminating point is reached, that is Sára or climax.

** ससन्देह—ससन्देहस्तु भेदोक्तौ तदनुक्तौ च संशयः।** When the difference is expressed (from a poet's point of view) or not expressed (there being a close resemblance) between two objects, that is Doubt or Sandeha.

** स्वभावोक्ति—**or Description according to Nature (also called Játi by some).—**स्वभावोक्तिस्तु हिम्भादेः स्वक्रियारूपवर्णनम्।** Svabha'vokti is the description of the peculiar action or posture **(रुपं वर्णः संस्थानं च)** of an object such as a child and the like. Of course the action &c. must be striking, such as is perceived by the poet alone.

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

**THE METRES USED IN THE PLAY.  
THEIR DEFINITIONS AND SCHEMES.**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-172415365844.png"/>

  1 The quantity of a syllable is determined by its vowel.A syllable with a short vowel is called **लघु** or light, and one with a long vowel is called **गुरु ** or heavy. But if a light syllable be followed by an Anuswa'ra or Visarga or by a conjunct consonant the syllable is made heavy. A syllable at the end of a quarter may be short or long according to necessity. **सानुस्वारश्व दीर्घश्व विसर्गी च गुरुर्भवेत्॥ वर्णः संयोगपूर्वश्व तथा पादान्तगोपि वा॥**

 2 A short syll. is marked as ~, and a long one as—.The following letters are symbols representing different triads **(गणऽ):--**

 ** य~ - -;र-~ - त- - ~ भ- ~ ~ ; ज ~ - ~ ; स~ ~ - ; म - - -न \~\~~ ग** represents a heavy syll and ल a light one.

 The following couplet will help the student in remembering the long and short syllables forming each Gana—**आदिमध्यावसानेषु यरता यान्ति लाघवम्। भजसा गौरवं यान्ति मनौ तु गुरुलाघवम्॥**

 3 The following are the metres occurring in this play, with their definitions and schemes:-

** अनुष्टुभ्—** or sloka is defined as—**पञ्चमं लघु सर्वत्र सप्तमं द्विचतुर्थयोः। गुरुषष्ठं च पादानां** **शेषेष्वनियमो मतः**॥ In Anushtubh the fifth syll. ought to be short and the sixth long in all quarters. The seventh should be short in the second and fourth quarters only. Other syllables are governed by no rule. I. 8, 12, 18; III. 1; V. 12, 21, 33; VI, 11; 1X. 41, 51, 52; X. 4, 7, 19, 22

** इन्द्रवज्रा—स्यादिन्द्रवज्रा यदि तौ जगौ गः।** Sch. of G. **त त ज ग ग.** I 4, 5, 33, III. 4, 11; IV. 5; VI. 1, 13.

** उपेन्द्रवज्रा—उपेन्द्रवज्रा जतजास्ततो गौ**। Sch. ज त ज ग ग. I. 10.

** उपजाति—अनन्तरोदीरितलक्ष्मभाजौ पादौ यदीयादुपजातयस्ताः।** A mixture of **इन्द्र.** and **उपेन्द्र** forms **उपजाति** III. 3; IX. 27.

** रथोद्धसा—रान्नराविह रथोद्धता लगौ** Sch. **र न र ल ग** (3. 8[^1348], or 4. 7) VIII. 3, 1X.21; X. 18.

[^1348]: # "The numerical figures indicate the casura or pause."

** शालिनी — मात्तौ गौ चेच्छालिनी वेदलोकैः**। Sch of G, **म त त ग ग**. (4 7) VI. 18; IX. 37.

** वियोगिनी—**also called **सुन्दरी** is a particular case of **वैतालीय्** (which is classed under Matravrittas) **विषमे ससजा गुरुः सम सभरा लोभ गुरुवियोगिनी**। This is an Ardhasamavrita, See **पुष्पि** ० below.

 Sch. **स स ज ग** (odd quarter)**; स भ र ल ग** (even q.) IX. 19.

** अपरवक्त्र—**(a particular kind of Vaita liya) **अयुजि ननरला गुरुः समे तदपरवक्त्रमिदं नजौ** **नरौ।** Sch. **न न ल ग** (odd quarter); **न ज ज र**. (oren g). IX. 23.

** औपच्छन्दसिक—**is the same as **वियोगिनी** with a long syll. added at the end; Sch., odd quarters **-स, स, ज, ग, ग**; even quartors—**स, भ, र, य.** III. 13.

** द्रुतविलम्बित—द्रुतविलम्बितमाह नभौ भरौ**। Sch**, न भ भ र.** (4, 8;or 4, 4, 4.). III. 10; IV. 7; VIII. 11; X. 16.

** वंशस्थ—जतौ तु वंशस्थमुदीरितं जरौ**। Soh of G**. ज त ज र**. VII.1; X. 6.

** पुष्पिताग्रा—अयुजिनयुगरेफतो यकारो युजि च नजौ जरगाश्च पुष्पिताग्रा**। Boh. **न न र य** (od. g.) **न ज ज र ग** (even q.) II. 6, 10; III. 15; V. 15; X. 2.

** प्रहर्षिणी—त्र्याशाभिर्मनजरगाः प्रहर्षिणीयम्**। Sob, **म न ज र ग** (3.10). 1. 37, 38; III. 17; IV. 1; V. 3, 25; IX. 14.

** मञ्जुभाषिणी—सजसा जगौ च यदि मञ्जुभाषिणी**। Sch. **स, ज, स, ख, ग,** (6-7). I. 39; II. 4; III. 7; V. 8; IX 9, 43, 48.

** वसन्ततिलका—उक्ता वसन्ततिलका तभजा जगौ गः**। Sch. **त, भ, ज,ज ग, ग.** I. 6, 9, 18, 19, 20, 21, 23, 25, 26, 29, 32, 34, 40; II. 8; III. 5; IV. 8; V. 27, 32, VI. 4, 8, 9, 12, 13, 14, 17, 20; VII. 2, 3, 4, VIII, 4, 5, 8, 12, 14; IX. 1, 2, 3, 13, 22, 31, 36, 40, 44, 47, 50, 54; X. 1, 9, 20, 21.

** मालिनी—ननमयययुतेयं मालिनी भोगिलोकैः**। Sch. न, न, म, य, य. (8.7.)

 I. 22, 24, 27, 28, 41; II. 9; III., 8, 14, 16; IV. 10; V. 1, 16; VIII. 1, 13, IX. 5, 6, 24, 28, 53; X. 8.

** पृथ्वी—जसौ जसयला वसुग्रहयतिश्च पृथ्वी गुरुः**। Sch. ज, स, ज, स, य, ल, ग. III. 13; VIII. 7; IX, 35, 38.

** मन्दाक्रान्ता—मन्दाक्रान्ताजलधिषडगैर्म्भो नतौ ताद्ररू चेत्**। Sch. **म, भ,न,त,त,ग ,ग.** 4, 6, 7.) I. 3, 15, 35; II, 5; III. 12; IV. 2, 20; VI. 2; VII. 5; VIII. 2; IX. 20, 25, 26, 46, X. 5.

** नर्दटक—यदि भवतो नजौ भजजला गुरुनर्दटकम्** \। Sch. **न, ज, भ, ज, ज, ल, ग,** (8. 9). V. 31; IX. 18.

** शिखरिणी—रसै रुद्रैश्छिन्ना यमनसभला गः शिखरिणी**। Sch. **य म न स, भ ल ग** (6. 11) I. 14, 16, 30, 31, II. 1, 3, 7, 11, 12, 13; III. 9, IV. 3, 4, 6, 9; V. 30, 34; VI. 7, 15; IX, 8, 29, 45,

** हरिणी—नसमरसला गः षड्वेदैर्हयैर्हरिणी मता**। Soh. **न. स, म, र, स.ल,ग**,(6, 4, 7,) I, 17, 36; II. 2; III. 2; V. 5, 26; VI. 6; IX. 10, 11, 12, 42, 15.

** शार्दुलविक्रीडित—सूर्याश्वैर्यदि मः सजो सततगाः शार्दूलविक्रीडितम्**। Sch. **म, स, ज, स, त, त,** **ग**. I. 2, 7; V. 2, 7, 9, 10, 11, 13, 14, 18, 19, 22, 24, 28, 29; VI. 3, 5, 19; VIII. 6, 9, 10; IX. 7, 15, 16, 17, 32, 33, 34, 39, X. 23, 24, 25.

** स्रग्धरा—म्रम्रैर्यार्ना त्रयेण त्रिमुनियतियुता स्रग्धरा कीर्तितेयम्।** Soh, **म, र, भ, न, य, य,** य. (7.7.7). I. 1, **पक्ष्माली** &c. ft. note ; V. 4, 6, 16, 17; IX, 30,

** दण्डक —**V. 23; See A Dic. Ap.

** आर्या—**This belongs to the class of metres regulated by the number of matra's or syllabic instants. **यस्याः पादे प्रथमे द्वादश मात्रास्तथा तृतीयेपि। अष्टादश द्वितीये चतुर्थके पञ्चदश** **सार्या** ॥ I. 11; VI. 10, IX, 4, 49; X. 3, 10, 11, 12, 14, 17.

**QUESTIONS FROM THE TEXT SET AT THE  
BOMBAY UNI. EXAMINATIONS.  
1869 (B. A.)**

 I Translate the following into English—**(a) प्रचलितकरिकृत्ति &c. V. 23. (b)प्रेङ्खद्भूरिमयूर** &c. VI. 5. Dissolve the first comp. in (a). 2 Explain the following, giving the context, and solve the conundrums:—**(a) स्नेहश्च निमित्तसव्यपेक्ष इति विप्रतिषिद्धमेतत्। (b) गुरुबाष्पस्तम्भमन्थरितकण्ठप्रतिलग्ननिश्वासमन्यादृशमेव भगवत्या वचनम्। (c) तस्यामभिनवो विचित्रः कुसुमेषुव्यापारः। (d) भगवत्येवंवादिनीत्याख्यायते। (e) प्रियं खलु युष्माकं मालतीजीवितं न पुनर्मालती। (f) सखि मदयन्तिके मालती प्रियसख्येवेदृश्यानि मन्त्रयितुं जानाति। (g) कं याचे यत्र तत्र ध्रुवमनवसरग्रस्त एवार्थिभावः। (h) एवंविधैर्विलसितैरतिबोधिसत्त्वैः**। Explain the technical terms in the following and give their ordinary senses:—(a) **निसृष्टार्थदूती कल्पस्तन्त्रयितव्यः।** (4) Is their any Patáká in Mâl. Mád. ? If so what is it, what is such a minor hero as Makaranda called in connection with such Patáká? Name and define the species of dramatic compositions to which the play you have read belongs, according to Hindu critics. 5 What evidence can you adduce from Mál. Mád, to prove that Bhav. knew of Kálidása and was acquainted with his works? State what ideas or passages in the play bear a very suspicious resemblance to the ideas or passages occurring in any of Káli's works. 6 Give the substance of the 6th and 9th Acts of Malati Mádhava. 7 Translate into English:— **परिच्छेदव्यक्तिर्भवति** &c. I. 31**. अद्यैवेन्दुमयूख** &c. VIII. 10. Explain the context of these passages.

1874 (B. A.)

 1 Translate, adding an explanation of the stanza in (a):—**(a) यत्सत्यमधुना** &c.**— लग्ना प्रिया।** P. 100 **(b) सावष्टम्भ—स्थिति।** V. 22. p. 109. (c) Dissolve and name the componnds in (b) (2) Explain the following, giving the context when necessary:—

 (**a) त्वमपि स्वभावेनैव—तासि p. 48 (b) वाक्प्रतिष्ठानिबन्धनानि—कैव। P. 89. (c) अयम॰—ते परिष्वङ्ग. p.195. (d) सुलभैव बुद्धरक्षिताप्रियसखी भवतः। (d) दिष्ट्या सुहृदबुद्ध्या वर्धितोसि मालत्या** **तदयमवसरः प्रीतिदायस्य**। One Ms. reads **मालत्याः;** which do you prefer and why? 3 (a) What is an Ankávatára ! Give an instance. (b) How many Rasas are there? Define and exemplify any one of them from the Mál, Mád. 1886\.

1 'There is more passion in the thoughts of Bhavabhuti than in those of Ka'lida'sa, but less fancy. There are few of the elegant similitudes in which the latter is so rich, and there is more that is common—place, and much that is strained and obscure. In none of his dramas does Bhavabhu'ti make any attempt at wit...On the other hand, he expatiates more largely in the description of pioturesque scenery and in the representation of human emotion, and is, perhaps entitled to even a higher place than his rival, as a poet. Discuss this remark of Wilson with particular reference to the Mál. Mád., giving quotations from the play to illustrate your answer. 2 Give the context of the following verses: —1 **अभिनव... लवलीलवङ्गयोरिव** &c. X. 3. 2 **प्रेयो मित्रं...** **जीवितं वा** &c.
